## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material. Temperature typically softens materials by reducing elastic modulus and flow stress, while strain determines the deformation response through elastic and/or plastic behavior.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus variation with temperature)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear plastic stress-strain relationship)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (power-law hardening with thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Hollomon with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law in both strain and temperature)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * (c3 * T)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 + c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal effect)
- Polynomial elastic: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic/hyperelastic)
- Linear thermal + nonlinear strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**3 (cubic elasticity with thermal modulus)
- Ludwik model: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (yield stress plus power-law hardening)
- Swift model with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (shifted power law with thermal effect)
- Ramberg-Osgood inverse: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 * epsilon**2 + 1)**(c2) (smooth elastic-plastic transition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of modulus → Stress scales with a linearly or exponentially decreasing function of temperature: (c0 - c1*T) or exp(-c2*T)
- Strain hardening saturation → Use of (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating stress approaches a plateau at large strains
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Sum of linear term (c0*epsilon) and power-law term (c1*epsilon**c2) with c2<1
- Temperature-strain separability → Multiplicative decomposition sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T) where strain and temperature effects are independent
- Yielding with offset strain → Shifted power law (epsilon + c0)**c1 to avoid singularity at zero strain
- Rubber-like hyperelasticity → Odd polynomial in strain: c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**3 + c2*epsilon**5 reflecting symmetric tension-compression
- Negative temperature sensitivity → Coefficient of T term is negative (c0 + c1*T with c1<0) reflecting material softening at high temperature
- Phase transition or anomaly → Non-monotonic temperature dependence may require quadratic T terms: c0 + c1*T + c2*T**2
